<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Radio frequency identification (RFID) systems have been increasingly gaining ground in massive utilization in many industrial, commercial, entertainment and other branches. Over the years, the UHF RFID systems have expanded from identification of bulky object (i.e., pallets) to smaller ones (boxes on the pallets) and even proceeded to the level of small items in boxes. The number of items in the range of reader increases rapidly and identified objects are getting smaller. This development makes great demands on small tag antennas with high radiation efficiency, which strongly affects the read range.</p><p>Performance properties of electrically small antennas (ESAs) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a> are determined by a fundamental rule that is frequently called the <i>Chu limit</i> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, which limits their minimum quality factor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-7" role="math" style="width: 0.904em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.72em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-8"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Q</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">Q</script></tex-math></inline-formula> that is inversely proportional to the bandwidth-efficiency product <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-10" role="math" style="width: 2.465em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.225em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.23em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-13"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-14" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">B</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">W</span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">η<span style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">{\rm BW}\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This is given by the expression <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-17" role="math" style="width: 10.754em; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.337em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">Q_{\min}=1/k^{3}a^{3}+1/ka</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-46" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); In case of nonspherical nonmagnetic ESA, the principal bound taking into account the antenna shape <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a> provides more appropriate values for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-50" role="math" style="width: 2.285em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1002.04em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-51"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-52"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.72em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-53" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Q</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-54"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-55"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-56" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">min</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">Q_{\min}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. These are computed using the relation <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-57" role="math" style="width: 11.414em; The value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-104" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.54em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-107" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">γ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.547em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-117" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≤</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-118" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">\gamma_{1}^{\rm norm}\leq 1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> implies larger <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-119" role="math" style="width: 2.285em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1002.04em 2.526em -999.997em); width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-123"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-124"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-125" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">min</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">Q_{\min}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and consequently lower <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-126" role="math" style="width: 3.486em; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 1.745em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-133"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-134"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-135" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">max</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">{\rm BW}_{\max}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for nonspherical geometries. Although the fundamental limitations cannot be broken, the performance improvement of RFID tag antennas as ESAs still represents an attractive topic of antenna research.</p><p>Apart from miniaturization, UHF RFID tag antennas for remote identification require a complex input impedance conjugate to the impedance of the integrated circuit used (IC or simply a chip), which is generally capacitive <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. The typical required ranges of real <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-136" role="math" style="width: 2.105em; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">R_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and imaginary <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-145" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-149"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-150"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-151" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">X_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> parts of antenna input impedance range from 15 to 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-154" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-155"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-156" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and from 100 to 400 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-157" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-158"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-159" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively. Methods used to achieve the required inductive input impedance typically comprise the use of folded dipole <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, multiple-arm folded dipole operated above the half-wavelength resonance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>, inductive coupled dipole spiral antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, or coupling the dipole to a small loop <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>. Loop-type antennas represent another applicable type of antenna. Basically, when made electrically small, they exhibit the required inductive input impedance. Antennas based on split rings (SRs) coupled with a small inner feeding loop were used in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>. The half-setup arrangement over the ground plane is presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a>. Multi-SR antennas were also investigated by the authors of this letter in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_1">[16]</a>.</p><p>In this letter, we investigate tag antennas composed of two and three concentric split rings (2-SR and 3-SR), where the inner ring is fed by an RFID chip; see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. An extensive systematic study of their achievable complex input impedance and radiation efficiency ranges for different electrical sizes is performed. The advantages of the proposed 3-SR over the standard 2-SR tag antenna for the given electrical size <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-160" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-161"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-162" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-163" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">ka</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is illustratively demonstrated using the Smith Chart. It is marked as the range of achievable input impedances together with the value of radiation efficiency, whereas the area delimited by a curved trapezoid denotes a typical range of required input impedance; see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(b)</a>. The selected 2-SR and 3-SR tag antennas matched to the particular impedance of an RFID chip are fabricated, and a detailed measurement of their impedance bandwidths and radiation properties is performed.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6450042/6450042-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6450042/6450042-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Sketch of 2-SR and 3-SR antenna geometry. In both cases, the inner SR is supposed to be fed by an RFID chip.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6450042/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Achievable Input Impedance and Radiation Efficiency of Electrically Small Double and Triple Split-Ring Antennas</h2></div><p>The application of the 2-SR antenna, consisting of a small internal loop (fed by a chip) coupled to an outer SR, represents an effective way of how to design a small tag antenna. The outer split ring is actually a curved dipole operating close to the half-wavelength resonance of the circumference <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-222" role="math" style="width: 4.147em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.727em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.67em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-223"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-224" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-225" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">∼</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-226" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.303em;">λ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-227"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-228"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-229" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-230" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">C \sim \lambda/2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with corresponding radius <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-231" role="math" style="width: 8.532em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 7.691em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1007.63em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-232"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-233" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-234" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-235" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.303em;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-236"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-237"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-238" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-239" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-240" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">π<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-241" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">∼</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-242" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.303em;">λ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-243"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-244"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-245" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-246" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">12</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">a = C/2\pi \sim \lambda/12</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It just meets the definition limit <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-247" role="math" style="width: 4.147em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.727em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.67em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-248"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-249" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-250" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-251" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-252" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.5</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">ka = 0.5</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for electrically small antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_2">[1]</a>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-253" role="math" style="width: 4.508em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.027em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.03em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-254"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-255" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-256" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-257" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-258" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">π<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-259"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-260"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-261" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-262" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">λ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">k = 2 \pi/\lambda</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the free-space wavenumber and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-263" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-264"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-265" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">a</script></tex-math></inline-formula> denotes radius of the smallest sphere enclosing the antenna. If such a 2-SR tag antenna is miniaturized below the given limit <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-266" role="math" style="width: 4.147em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.727em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.67em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-267"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-268" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-269" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-270" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-271" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.5</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">ka = 0.5</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the range of its achievable complex input impedance is limited (see the text below). To explore the influence of an additional SR on the extension of achievable input impedance range, we made a performance comparison study of an extensive set of 2-SR and 3-SR tag antennas. All results were achieved by the electromagnetic (EM) simulator IE3D based on a method of moments.</p><p>To exhibit performance of the geometry, the structures are investigated without supporting dielectric substrate at the frequency of 869 MHz that is chosen to fit into the European UHF RFID band. In the case of the 3-SR version, both gaps are chosen to be identical, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-457" role="math" style="width: 8.471em; In other words, it concerns the variations of values <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-492" role="math" style="width: 7.691em; By virtue of inclusion of structures with thinner strips or slots between them, the said numerous simulations were extended by all geometries where each parameter is changed with a smaller step (0.4 mm).</p><p>The results of a large number of simulations are presented as a “cloud” of input impedances in the Smith Chart for decreasing electrical size; see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>. \eta_{r} &gt; 50\hbox{\%}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Geometries with radiation efficiency lower than 50% are not included in the Smith Chart because their introduction would reduce transparency of the pictures.</p><p>We found the smallest electrical size <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-577" role="math" style="width: 4.688em; see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a>. Further miniaturization shifts the impedance “cloud” toward the rim of the Smith Chart, and for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-588" role="math" style="width: 4.147em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.727em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.73em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-589"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-590" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-591" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-592" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&lt;</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-593" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.4</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">ka &lt; 0.4</script></tex-math></inline-formula> [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(b)</a>], the “cloud” moves completely out of the requested area. The smaller the antenna dimensions, the more significant the reduction in the radiation efficiency. Even for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-594" role="math" style="width: 4.147em; 80\hbox{\%}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The maximum simulated radiating efficiency reached <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-617" role="math" style="width: 5.348em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.808em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.75em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-618"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-619"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-620" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">η<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-621"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-622"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-623" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-624" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-625" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">90.7</span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-626"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-627"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-628" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">%</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">\eta_{\rm r} = 90.7\hbox{\%}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Given these results, it can be argued that the major issue of the small 2-SR antenna consists in the impossibility to cover the whole required impedance area. Therefore, the 2-SR tag antenna that is smaller than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-629" role="math" style="width: 4.147em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.727em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.73em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-630"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-631" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-632" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-633" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-634" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.4</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">ka = 0.4</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is unsuitable for matching to typical UHF RFID chips.</p><p>For further possible miniaturization of the SR-type tag antenna, we implemented and investigated the version involving three split rings (3-SR). Although in this case, the number of possible geometries increases rapidly, the setting of THE parameter sweep (i.e., the step, including dimensions of 0.4 mm and the low limit for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-635" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.14em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-636"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-637"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-638" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-639"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-640"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-641" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-642" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">r_{\rm in}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) was preserved. The additional SR significantly affects the achievable range of input impedances. Although for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-643" role="math" style="width: 4.147em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.727em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.73em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-644"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-645" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-646" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-647" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-648" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.4</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">ka = 0.4</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the input impedance of thr 2-SR structure remains at the rim of the Smith Chart [<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(b)</a>], input impedances of a 3-SR antenna of the same size completely fills in, again, the required impedance area [<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(c)</a>]. The additional SR thus enables a further miniaturization of this type of antenna.</p><p>For both 2-SR and 3-SR structures, the number of bullet marks in the impedance “cloud” is dropping provided that the size <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-649" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-650"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-651" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-652" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">ka</script></tex-math></inline-formula> decreases. This phenomenon originates from the fall of radiation efficiency below <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-653" role="math" style="width: 4.568em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.087em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.03em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-654"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-655"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-656" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">η<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-657"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-658"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-659"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-660"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-661" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-662" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-663" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">50</span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-664"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-665"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-666" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">%</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">\eta _{{\rm r}}= 50\hbox{\%}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (these structures are excluded from the chart). The miniaturization limit of 3-SR antennas found by systematic investigation of the above specified range of geometries is about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-667" role="math" style="width: 4.688em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.207em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-668"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-669" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-670" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-671" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-672" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.29</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">ka = 0.29</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-673" role="math" style="width: 3.246em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.886em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.83em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-674"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-675" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-676" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-677" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">16</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">a = 16 </script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm at 869MHz), which means that the impedance “cloud” shifted the rim of Smith Chart, and it is impossible to cover the whole required impedance range with the efficiency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-678" role="math" style="width: 4.568em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.087em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.03em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-679"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-680"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-681" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">η<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-682"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-683"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-684" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-685" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&gt;</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-686" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">50</span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-687"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-688"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-689" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">%</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">\eta_{\rm r} &gt; 50\hbox{\%}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Such findings are helpful for proper selection of the tag antenna geometry when small size and particular complex input impedance have to be concurrently achieved.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6450042/6450042-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6450042/6450042-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>(a), (b) Simulated vector current density distribution and (c), (d) respective radiation patterns for total electric field of 2-SR and 3-SR antennas at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-690" role="math" style="width: 4.038em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.178em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1003.11em 2.649em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-691"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-692" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.069em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-693" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-694" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">869</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.338em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">f = 869</script></tex-math></inline-formula> MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6450042/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The current density distributions of small 2-SR and 3-SR antennas are depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a) and (b)</a>. The currents on the outer split ring(s) obviously flow in the direction concurrent with the inner loop so that the respective radiation patterns correspond to the radiation of a small loop with constant current distribution along its perimeter, providing a nearly omnidirectional pattern in the plane of antenna motifs; see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(c) and (d)</a>.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Parameters of Fabricated Split-Ring Antennas</h2></div><p>In order to verify real impedance and radiation parameters of investigated antennas, two samples of 2-SR and 3-SR UHF tag antennas were manufactured (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>) on a thin Taconic TLP-3 substrate of the height <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-695" role="math" style="width: 4.688em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.207em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.21em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-696"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-697" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-698" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-699" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.127</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">h = 0.127 </script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm (its relative permittivity equals <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-700" role="math" style="width: 4.508em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.027em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.97em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-701"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-702"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-703" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ε</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-704"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-705"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-706" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-707" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-708" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2.33</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">\varepsilon _{\rm r} = 2.33</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and loss tangent is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-709" role="math" style="width: 6.069em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.468em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.41em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-710"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-711"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-712"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-713" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-714" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-715" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">δ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-716" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-717" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.0009</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">{\rm tg} \delta = 0.0009</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 10 GHz), both closely matched to the chip input impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-718" role="math" style="width: 9.432em; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-719"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-720"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-722"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-723"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-724" style="font-size: 70.7%; The measurement of tag antenna input impedance was performed in the half-loop arrangement with the ground plane size of 145×145 mm<sup>2</sup>; i.e., 0.42 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-737" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; <p></p><p>The measured input impedance has to be subsequently compared to the half of chip impedance; i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-749" role="math" style="width: 9.973em; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-750"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-751"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-752" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-758" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">p</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-759"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-760"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-761" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-762" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-763" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-764" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">8</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-765" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">Z_{\rm chip}/2 = 8 - {\rm j}175\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>; which stands for the analogy between dipole and monopole arrangements.</p><p>Their geometrical and simulated and measured parameters are depicted in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Tables I</a> and <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">II</a>, respectively.

<p></p><p>The radiation efficiency was measured with the help of the Wheeler cap method <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_3">[17]</a>, where the cap size amounted to 120×120×120 mm<sup>3</sup>. The fractional half-power impedance bandwidth was determined from the curve of power transmission coefficient (taking into account half-loop arrangement), evaluated from the measured complex antenna input impedance; <div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>Although the double split-ring antenna with electrical size of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-889" role="math" style="width: 4.147em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.727em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.67em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-890"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-891" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-892" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-893" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">∼</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-894" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.5</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-77">ka \sim 0.5</script></tex-math></inline-formula> meets the requirement of an electrically small antenna, its practical utilization as a UHF RFID tag antenna is limited only to structures with electrical size of approximately <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-78-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-895" role="math" style="width: 4.688em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.207em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.21em 2.526em -999.997em); overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-78">ka \geq 0.47</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-79-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-901" role="math" style="width: 5.288em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.748em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.63em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-902"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-903" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-904" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-905" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.246em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.19em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-942"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-943"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-944"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-945" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-946" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">400</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-947" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-948" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">{-}400\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>).</p><p>As it has been observed from the systematic EM simulation of the large set of antenna configurations showing the electrical radius within the range <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-949" role="math" style="width: 7.631em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.85em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.79em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-950"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-951" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.25</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-952" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≤</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-953" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.303em;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-954" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-955" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≤</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-956" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.5</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-85">0.25\leq ka\leq 0.5</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the implementation of an additional third split ring enables a further reduction of the outer electrical size as far as to approximately <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-86-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-957" role="math" style="width: 10.273em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 9.252em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1009.13em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-958"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-959" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-960" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-961" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-962" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.29</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-963" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-964" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-965" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-966" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-967" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.303em;">λ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-968"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-969"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-970" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-971" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">21</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-972" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-86">ka = 0.29\ (a = \lambda /21)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. At the same time, it is possible to maintain the required range of input impedances above this size as well as the sufficiently high radiation efficiency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-973" role="math" style="width: 5.408em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.868em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.75em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-974"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-975" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-976"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-977" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">η<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-978"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-979"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-980" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-981" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&gt;</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-982" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">50</span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-983"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-984"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-985" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">%</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-986" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-87">(\eta_{r} &gt; 50\hbox{\%})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This finding might be helpful for selection of proper structure within split-ring-type antenna structures, provided that the miniaturization is demanded as a key feature.</p><p>Although the impedance bandwidth is quite narrow, the investigated tag antennas sufficiently cover the European UHF RFID band of 865–869 MHz.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
